{\\n659: \\tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\\n660: \\t\\treturn numAllNodes\\n661: \\t}\\n662: \\n663: \\t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: \t\tfwk.EventRecorder().Eventf(pod, nil, v1.EventTypeWarning, \"FailedScheduling\", \"Scheduling\", \"skip schedule deleting pod: %v/%v\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name)\n371: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes() == 0 {\n399: \t\treturn result, ErrNoNodesAvailable\n400: \t}\n401: \n402: \tfeasibleNodes, diagnosis, err := sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)\n403: \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, diagnosis framework.Diagnosis) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n530: \tnnn := nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\n65: type GVK string\n66: \n67: // Constants for GVKs.\n68: const (\n69: \t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\n70: \t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\n71: \t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\n72: \t//           - a Pod that is deleted\n73: \t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\n74: \t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\n75: \tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n76: \t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\n77: \t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n78: \t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n79: \t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n80: \t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n81: \t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LLaTfi54XAsJAfNSBi4LmD","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01VRF4cR95EkbuqkTL6iNMoH","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Bug Analysis: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Examined to identify GVK constants available in framework\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — Examined for EventsToRegister() implementation and Filter() method\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Examined to understand how event handlers are registered based on GVK list\n- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — Examined for unionedGVKs() function that builds event handler map\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point to understand how scheduling failures trigger re-queueing\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 112 (`ScheduleOne()` method)\n   - When `schedulingCycle()` fails with `Unschedulable` status, `FailureHandler()` is called\n\n2. **FailureHandler calls**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 1068 (`handleSchedulingFailure()`)\n   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Queue re-evaluation triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 377 (`buildEvtResHandler()`)\n   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods\n\n4. **Events come from**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 395 (switch statement on `gvkMap`)\n   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`\n\n5. **gvkMap built by**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` line 525 (`unionedGVKs()` function)\n   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins\n\n6. **Events declared in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 381 (`EventsToRegister()`)\n   - Lists all events that should trigger pod re-evaluation when plugin rejects a pod\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 1139 (`nodeIsSuitable()`)\n   - Filter method fails when checking if a node has suitable resources (returns Unschedulable)\n   - This happens when no ResourceSlices exist yet\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Primary Issue (Line ~95 in types.go)**: ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant in the framework\n\n**Secondary Issue (Lines 381-412 in dynamicresources.go)**: ResourceSlice is not included in EventsToRegister()\n\n**Tertiary Issue (Lines 395-492 in eventhandlers.go)**: No case for framework.ResourceSlice in the event handler registration switch statement\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a **race condition in the event-driven queue re-evaluation system**:\n\n1. **The Problem**: When a pod requesting DRA devices arrives before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler marks the pod as Unschedulable because:\n   - The dynamicresources Filter plugin calls `nodeIsSuitable()`\n   - This function queries the ResourceSlices to determine if a node has suitable resources\n   - Since no ResourceSlices exist yet, the check fails and returns Unschedulable\n\n2. **Why the Pod Gets Stuck**: When ResourceSlices are created/updated after the pod is unschedulable:\n   - **ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant** in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Therefore, it cannot be used in the dynamicresources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method\n   - Without being registered, ResourceSlice events are never added to the `gvkMap`\n   - Without being in `gvkMap`, the scheduler's event handler registration code in `eventhandlers.go` never creates event handlers for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Without event handlers, ResourceSlice creation/update events are **silently dropped**\n   - The unschedulable pod is never moved to the activeQ for re-evaluation\n\n3. **Why This Happens**:\n   - The DynamicResourceAllocation (DRA) feature was added without completing the event handler integration\n   - ResourceSlice is a valid Kubernetes resource (resource.k8s.io/v1alpha2) but was never added to the framework's GVK constants\n   - The plugin's EventsToRegister() can only register events for GVKs defined in the framework\n\n### Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\nPod arrives (no ResourceSlices yet)\n    ↓\nschedulingCycle() → SchedulePod()\n    ↓\ndynamicresources.Filter() checks nodeIsSuitable()\n    ↓\nnodeIsSuitable() queries ResourceSlices (finds none)\n    ↓\nFilter returns Unschedulable → Pod added to unschedulablePodPool\n    ↓\nDRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice\n    ↓\nResourceSlice event occurs ❌ BUT...\n    ❌ No GVK defined for ResourceSlice in framework/types.go\n    ❌ Therefore, not in dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()\n    ❌ Therefore, not in gvkMap\n    ❌ Therefore, no event handler registered\n    ❌ Event is silently dropped\n    ↓\nPod remains in unschedulablePodPool FOREVER ❌\n```\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (after line 95)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (after line 492)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n \t\t\tif at&framework.Add != 0 {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Storage().V1().StorageClasses().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n```\n\n### 4. Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod requesting a resource may become schedulable when a ResourceSlice is created\n+\t\t// or updated with suitable resources for the node.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 5. Add QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice Changes\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 564 or at end of file before PostBind)\n\n```go\n// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange checks whether a ResourceSlice change makes an unschedulable pod schedulable.\n// A pod waiting for resource allocation may be schedulable once ResourceSlices are available with suitable resources.\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\t// Check if this pod uses dynamic resources\n\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, nil); err != nil {\n\t\t// Pod doesn't use any ResourceClaims or cannot be scheduled\n\t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// ResourceSlice changes might make this pod schedulable, so always queue it\n\t// (conservative approach since we can't easily determine which pod depends on which ResourceSlice)\n\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"ResourceSlice was added or updated, requeuing pod that uses dynamic resources\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why This Bug Occurs\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where:\n\n1. **Plugins declare events** via `EventsToRegister()` that should trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods\n2. **The scheduler collects these events** and builds a map of GVK → ActionType\n3. **Event handlers are registered** only for GVKs present in this map\n4. **When events occur**, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate pods\n\nThe DRA feature was added but **ResourceSlice was never added to the framework's GVK constants**. This means:\n- It cannot be declared in EventsToRegister()\n- It is never added to the event handler registration map\n- No handlers are registered for it\n- Events are silently dropped\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThis is a **silent failure** — no errors are logged, but pods get permanently stuck:\n- The scheduler correctly marks the pod as Unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist)\n- The pod should be re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available\n- But the re-evaluation never happens because the event is never delivered\n- The operator sees a pod stuck in Pending state indefinitely\n\n### Severity\n\n**Critical** — Pods requesting DRA resources will be permanently stuck if:\n1. A pod is created before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n2. This will work around the bug if pods are created after ResourceSlices exist\n3. But race conditions make this unpredictable in production\n\n### Fix Scope\n\nThe fix is minimal and consists of:\n1. Adding one GVK constant\n2. Adding one entry to the wildcard resource list\n3. Adding one case in the event handler switch statement\n4. Adding one event entry in the plugin's EventsToRegister()\n5. When `schedulingCycle()` fails with `Unschedulable` status, `FailureHandler()` is called\n\n2. **FailureHandler calls**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 1068 (`handleSchedulingFailure()`)\n   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Queue re-evaluation triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 377 (`buildEvtResHandler()`)\n   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods\n\n4. **Events come from**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 395 (switch statement on `gvkMap`)\n   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`\n\n5. **gvkMap built by**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` line 525 (`unionedGVKs()` function)\n   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins\n\n6. **Events declared in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 381 (`EventsToRegister()`)\n   - Lists all events that should trigger pod re-evaluation when plugin rejects a pod\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 1139 (`nodeIsSuitable()`)\n   - Filter method fails when checking if a node has suitable resources (returns Unschedulable)\n   - This happens when no ResourceSlices exist yet\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Primary Issue (Line ~95 in types.go)**: ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant in the framework\n\n**Secondary Issue (Lines 381-412 in dynamicresources.go)**: ResourceSlice is not included in EventsToRegister()\n\n**Tertiary Issue (Lines 395-492 in eventhandlers.go)**: No case for framework.ResourceSlice in the event handler registration switch statement\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a **race condition in the event-driven queue re-evaluation system**:\n\n1. **The Problem**: When a pod requesting DRA devices arrives before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler marks the pod as Unschedulable because:\n   - The dynamicresources Filter plugin calls `nodeIsSuitable()`\n   - This function queries the ResourceSlices to determine if a node has suitable resources\n   - Since no ResourceSlices exist yet, the check fails and returns Unschedulable\n\n2. **Why the Pod Gets Stuck**: When ResourceSlices are created/updated after the pod is unschedulable:\n   - **ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant** in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Therefore, it cannot be used in the dynamicresources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method\n   - Without being registered, ResourceSlice events are never added to the `gvkMap`\n   - Without being in `gvkMap`, the scheduler's event handler registration code in `eventhandlers.go` never creates event handlers for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Without event handlers, ResourceSlice creation/update events are **silently dropped**\n   - The unschedulable pod is never moved to the activeQ for re-evaluation\n\n3. **Why This Happens**:\n   - The DynamicResourceAllocation (DRA) feature was added without completing the event handler integration\n   - ResourceSlice is a valid Kubernetes resource (resource.k8s.io/v1alpha2) but was never added to the framework's GVK constants\n   - The plugin's EventsToRegister() can only register events for GVKs defined in the framework\n\n### Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\nPod arrives (no ResourceSlices yet)\n    ↓\nschedulingCycle() → SchedulePod()\n    ↓\ndynamicresources.Filter() checks nodeIsSuitable()\n    ↓\nnodeIsSuitable() queries ResourceSlices (finds none)\n    ↓\nFilter returns Unschedulable → Pod added to unschedulablePodPool\n    ↓\nDRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice\n    ↓\nResourceSlice event occurs ❌ BUT...\n    ❌ No GVK defined for ResourceSlice in framework/types.go\n    ❌ Therefore, not in dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()\n    ❌ Therefore, not in gvkMap\n    ❌ Therefore, no event handler registered\n    ❌ Event is silently dropped\n    ↓\nPod remains in unschedulablePodPool FOREVER ❌\n```\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (after line 95)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (after line 492)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n \t\t\tif at&framework.Add != 0 {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Storage().V1().StorageClasses().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n```\n\n### 4. Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod requesting a resource may become schedulable when a ResourceSlice is created\n+\t\t// or updated with suitable resources for the node.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 5. Add QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice Changes\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 564 or at end of file before PostBind)\n\n```go\n// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange checks whether a ResourceSlice change makes an unschedulable pod schedulable.\n// A pod waiting for resource allocation may be schedulable once ResourceSlices are available with suitable resources.\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\t// Check if this pod uses dynamic resources\n\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, nil); err != nil {\n\t\t// Pod doesn't use any ResourceClaims or cannot be scheduled\n\t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// ResourceSlice changes might make this pod schedulable, so always queue it\n\t// (conservative approach since we can't easily determine which pod depends on which ResourceSlice)\n\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"ResourceSlice was added or updated, requeuing pod that uses dynamic resources\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why This Bug Occurs\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where:\n\n1. **Plugins declare events** via `EventsToRegister()` that should trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods\n2. **The scheduler collects these events** and builds a map of GVK → ActionType\n3. **Event handlers are registered** only for GVKs present in this map\n4. **When events occur**, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate pods\n\nThe DRA feature was added but **ResourceSlice was never added to the framework's GVK constants**. This means:\n- It cannot be declared in EventsToRegister()\n- It is never added to the event handler registration map\n- No handlers are registered for it\n- Events are silently dropped\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThis is a **silent failure** — no errors are logged, but pods get permanently stuck:\n- The scheduler correctly marks the pod as Unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist)\n- The pod should be re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available\n- But the re-evaluation never happens because the event is never delivered\n- The operator sees a pod stuck in Pending state indefinitely\n\n### Severity\n\n**Critical** — Pods requesting DRA resources will be permanently stuck if:\n1. A pod is created before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n2. This will work around the bug if pods are created after ResourceSlices exist\n3. But race conditions make this unpredictable in production\n\n### Fix Scope\n\nThe fix is minimal and consists of:\n1. Adding one GVK constant\n2. Adding one entry to the wildcard resource list\n3. Adding one case in the event handler switch statement\n4. Adding one event entry in the plugin's EventsToRegister()\n5. Adding one optional QueueingHintFn for efficiency\n\nThe fix is **backward compatible** and introduces no breaking changes.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

This means:\n   208→- It cannot be declared in EventsToRegister()\n   209→- It is never added to the event handler registration map\n   210→- No handlers are registered for it\n   211→- Events are silently dropped\n   212→\n   213→### Why This Matters\n   214→\n   215→This is a **silent failure** — no errors are logged, but pods get permanently stuck:\n   216→- The scheduler correctly marks the pod as Unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist)\n   217→- The pod should be re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available\n   218→- But the re-evaluation never happens because the event is never delivered\n   219→- The operator sees a pod stuck in Pending state indefinitely\n   220→\n   221→### Severity\n   222→\n   223→**Critical** — Pods requesting DRA resources will be permanently stuck if:\n   224→1. A pod is created before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n   225→2. This will work around the bug if pods are created after ResourceSlices exist\n   226→3. But race conditions make this unpredictable in production\n   227→\n   228→### Fix Scope\n   229→\n   230→The fix is minimal and consists of:\n   231→1. Adding one GVK constant\n   232→2. Adding one entry to the wildcard resource list\n   233→3. Adding one case in the event handler switch statement\n   234→4. Adding one event entry in the plugin's EventsToRegister()\n   235→5. Adding one optional QueueingHintFn for efficiency\n   236→\n   237→The fix is **backward compatible** and introduces no breaking changes.\n   238→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. When `schedulingCycle()` fails with `Unschedulable` status, `FailureHandler()` is called\n\n2. **FailureHandler calls**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 1068 (`handleSchedulingFailure()`)\n   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Queue re-evaluation triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 377 (`buildEvtResHandler()`)\n   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods\n\n4. **Events come from**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 395 (switch statement on `gvkMap`)\n   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`\n\n5. **gvkMap built by**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` line 525 (`unionedGVKs()` function)\n   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins\n\n6. **Events declared in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 381 (`EventsToRegister()`)\n   - Lists all events that should trigger pod re-evaluation when plugin rejects a pod\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 1139 (`nodeIsSuitable()`)\n   - Filter method fails when checking if a node has suitable resources (returns Unschedulable)\n   - This happens when no ResourceSlices exist yet\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Primary Issue (Line ~95 in types.go)**: ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant in the framework\n\n**Secondary Issue (Lines 381-412 in dynamicresources.go)**: ResourceSlice is not included in EventsToRegister()\n\n**Tertiary Issue (Lines 395-492 in eventhandlers.go)**: No case for framework.ResourceSlice in the event handler registration switch statement\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a **race condition in the event-driven queue re-evaluation system**:\n\n1. **The Problem**: When a pod requesting DRA devices arrives before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler marks the pod as Unschedulable because:\n   - The dynamicresources Filter plugin calls `nodeIsSuitable()`\n   - This function queries the ResourceSlices to determine if a node has suitable resources\n   - Since no ResourceSlices exist yet, the check fails and returns Unschedulable\n\n2. **Why the Pod Gets Stuck**: When ResourceSlices are created/updated after the pod is unschedulable:\n   - **ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant** in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Therefore, it cannot be used in the dynamicresources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method\n   - Without being registered, ResourceSlice events are never added to the `gvkMap`\n   - Without being in `gvkMap`, the scheduler's event handler registration code in `eventhandlers.go` never creates event handlers for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Without event handlers, ResourceSlice creation/update events are **silently dropped**\n   - The unschedulable pod is never moved to the activeQ for re-evaluation\n\n3. **Why This Happens**:\n   - The DynamicResourceAllocation (DRA) feature was added without completing the event handler integration\n   - ResourceSlice is a valid Kubernetes resource (resource.k8s.io/v1alpha2) but was never added to the framework's GVK constants\n   - The plugin's EventsToRegister() can only register events for GVKs defined in the framework\n\n### Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\nPod arrives (no ResourceSlices yet)\n    ↓\nschedulingCycle() → SchedulePod()\n    ↓\ndynamicresources.Filter() checks nodeIsSuitable()\n    ↓\nnodeIsSuitable() queries ResourceSlices (finds none)\n    ↓\nFilter returns Unschedulable → Pod added to unschedulablePodPool\n    ↓\nDRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice\n    ↓\nResourceSlice event occurs ❌ BUT...\n    ❌ No GVK defined for ResourceSlice in framework/types.go\n    ❌ Therefore, not in dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()\n    ❌ Therefore, not in gvkMap\n    ❌ Therefore, no event handler registered\n    ❌ Event is silently dropped\n    ↓\nPod remains in unschedulablePodPool FOREVER ❌\n```\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (after line 95)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Here's a summary of the investigation:\n\n## Summary\n\n**Root Cause**: The Kubernetes scheduler's event-driven re-queueing system is missing support for ResourceSlice events, causing pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices to become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created.\n\n**The Bug Chain**:\n1. Pod arrives requesting DRA resources (no ResourceSlices exist yet)\n2. `dynamicresources.Filter()` returns Unschedulable → pod moved to unschedulable queue\n3. DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n4. **BUG**: ResourceSlice events are silently dropped because:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT defined as a GVK constant in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Cannot be registered in `dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()`\n   - Not added to event handler registration map (`gvkMap`)\n   - No event handlers are registered for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Events are never delivered → pod never re-evaluated\n\n**Proposed Fix**: 5 minimal code changes across 2 files:\n1. Add ResourceSlice GVK constant to framework types\n2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() \n3. Register ResourceSlice event handler in eventhandlers.go\n4. Register ResourceSlice events in dynamicresources plugin\n5.
